<p>The <b>federal subjects of Russia</b>, also referred to as the <b>subjects of the Russian Federation</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">субъекты Российской Федерации</span> <i>subyekty Rossiyskoy Federatsii</i>) or simply as the <b>subjects of the federation</b> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">субъекты федерации</span> <i>subyekty federatsii</i>), are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constituent_entity" title="Constituent entity">constituent entities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, its top-level political divisions according to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Since March 18, 2014, the Russian Federation constitutionally consists of 85 federal subjects,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution65_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution65-2">[2]</a></sup> although the two most recently added subjects are internationally recognized as part of <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Treaty_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Treaty-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the Russian Constitution, the Russian Federation consists of republics, krais, oblasts, cities of federal importance, an autonomous oblast, and autonomous okrugs, all of which are equal subjects of the Russian Federation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Three <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">Russian cities of federal importance</a> have a status of both city and separate federal subject which comprises other cities and towns (<a href="/wiki/Zelenograd" title="Zelenograd">Zelenograd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Troitsk,_Moscow" title="Troitsk, Moscow">Troitsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">Kronstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kolpino,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Kolpino, Saint Petersburg">Kolpino</a>, etc.) within federal city keeping old structure of postal address. In 1993, there were 89 federal subjects listed. By 2008, the number of federal subjects had been decreased to 83 because of several <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia#Mergers" title="Federal subjects of Russia">mergers</a>. In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> became the 84th and 85th federal subjects of Russia.</p>
<p>Every federal subject has its own <a href="/wiki/Governor_(Russia)" title="Governor (Russia)">head</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Regional_parliaments_of_Russia" title="Regional parliaments of Russia">parliament</a>, and a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Constitutional_(charter)_court_of_a_subject_of_the_Russian_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Constitutional (charter) court of a subject of the Russian Federation (page does not exist)">constitutional court</a>. Federal subjects have their own constitution and legislation. Subjects have equal rights in relations with federal government bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The federal subjects have equal representation—two delegates each—in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_Council_of_Russia" title="Federation Council of Russia">Federation Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Russia" title="Federal Assembly of Russia">Federal Assembly</a>. They do, however, differ in the degree of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" title="Autonomous area">autonomy</a> they enjoy (<a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_federalism" title="Asymmetric federalism">asymmetric federalism</a>).</p>
<p>Composition of post-Soviet Russia was formed during the history of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> within the USSR and didn't change in the moment of dissolution of the USSR. In 1992 during so-called "parade of sovereignties", <a href="/wiki/Nationalisms_in_Russia" title="Nationalisms in Russia">separatist sentiments</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Laws" title="War of Laws">War of Laws</a> within Russia, the Russian regions signed the Federation Treaty (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">Федеративный договор</span> <i>Federativny Dogovor</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> establishing and regulating the current inner composition of Russia, based on division of authorities and powers among Russian government bodies and government bodies of constituent entities. The Federation Treaty was included in the text of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1978" title="Russian Constitution of 1978">1978 Constitution of the Russian SFSR</a>. The current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a> was adopted by national referendum, came into force on <span class="mw-formatted-date" title="1993-12-25">December 25, 1993</span> and abolished the model of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_republic_(system_of_government)" title="Soviet republic (system of government)">Soviet system of government</a> introduced in 1918 by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> based on right to secede from the country and unlimited sovereignty of federal subjects (in practice it was never allowed), which conflicts with country's integrity and federal laws. The new constitution eliminated a number of legal conflicts, reserved rights of the regions, introduced the institute of local self-government and didn't grant Soviet-time right to secede from the country. In the late 1990s and early 2000s, the political system became de jure closer to other modern <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal states with a republican form of government</a> in the world. In the 2000s, according to the policy of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Russia" title="United Russia">United Russia</a> party (<a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant party</a> in all federal subjects), the Russian parliament changed the distribution of tax revenues, reduced the number of elections in the regions and gave more power to the federal authorities.</p>
<p>There are several groupings of Russian regions. Federal subjects should not be confused with the eight <i><a href="/wiki/Federal_districts_of_Russia" title="Federal districts of Russia">Federal districts</a></i> which are not subdivisions of Russia, are much larger and each encompass many federal subjects. Federal districts were created by <a href="/wiki/Decree_of_the_President_of_Russia" title="Decree of the President of Russia">Executive Order of the President of Russia</a> specially for <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Administration_of_Russia" title="Presidential Administration of Russia">presidential envoys</a>. <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Russia" title="Time in Russia">Time zones</a> are defined by the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Government_of_Russia" title="Order of the Government of Russia">Order of the federal government</a>, the composition of Judicial districts is defined by the federal law "On arbitration courts", <a href="/wiki/Economic_regions_of_Russia" title="Economic regions of Russia">Economic regions</a> are administrated by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Economic_Development_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Economic Development (Russia)">Ministry of Economic Development</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Defense (Russia)">Ministry of Defense</a> uses the terminology of <a href="/wiki/Military_districts_of_Russia" title="Military districts of Russia">Military districts</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_subjects_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>An official government translation of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a> in Article 5 states:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> "1. The Russian Federation shall consist of <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">republics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krais_of_Russia" title="Krais of Russia">krays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oblasts_of_Russia" title="Oblasts of Russia">oblasts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">cities of federal significance</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_oblasts_of_Russia" title="Autonomous oblasts of Russia">autonomous oblast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_okrugs_of_Russia" title="Autonomous okrugs of Russia">autonomous okrugs</a>, which shall have equal rights as constituent entities of the Russian Federation."</p>
<p>Another translation of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a> gives for article 65: "<i>The Russian Federation includes the following subjects of the Russian Federation:</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution.ru_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-constitution.ru-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>How to translate the Russian term was discussed during the 49th annual <a href="/wiki/American_Translators_Association" title="American Translators Association">American Translators Association</a> conference in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orlando" title="Orlando">Orlando</a>, in which Tom Fennel, a freelance translator, argued that the term "constituent entity of the Russian Federation" should be preferred to "subject".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> This recommendation is also shared by Tamara Nekrasova, Head of Translation Department, Goltsblat BLP, who in her "Traps &amp; Mishaps in Legal Translation" presentation in Paris stated that "<i>constituent entity of the Russian Federation</i> is more appropriate than <i>subject of the Russian Federation</i> (subject would be OK for a monarchy)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_subjects_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_(2014).svg" title="Federal subjects of Russia"><img alt="Federal subjects of Russia" data-file-height="936" data-file-width="1608" height="402" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/690px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/1035px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/1380px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png 2x" width="690"/></a></div>
</div>
<p>Each federal subject belongs to one of the following types:</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable">
<tr>
<th>Legend</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFEC77; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 46 <a href="/wiki/Oblasts_of_Russia" title="Oblasts of Russia">oblasts</a></div>
</td>
<td>most common type of federal subjects with a governor and locally elected legislature. Commonly named after their administrative centers.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00C160; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 22 <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">republics</a></div>
</td>
<td>nominally<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> autonomous, each has its own constitution and legislature; is represented by the federal government in international affairs; is meant to be home to a specific ethnic minority.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF9400; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 9 <a href="/wiki/Krais_of_Russia" title="Krais of Russia">krais</a></div>
</td>
<td>essentially the same as oblasts. The title "territory" is historic, originally given because they were once considered frontier regions.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #006989; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 4 <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_okrugs_of_Russia" title="Autonomous okrugs of Russia">autonomous okrugs</a></div>
</td>
<td>with substantial or predominant ethnic minority</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF0037; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 3 <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal cities</a></div>
</td>
<td>major cities that function as separate regions.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C300FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_oblasts_of_Russia" title="Autonomous oblasts of Russia">autonomous oblast</a></div>
</td>
<td>the only autonomous oblast is the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Jewish Autonomous Oblast">Jewish Autonomous Oblast</a></td>
</tr>
</table>

<div class="refbegin" style=""><b>a.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_anone"><a href="#ref_anone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> The largest city is also listed when it is different from the capital/administrative center.</div>
<p><b>b.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bnone"><a href="#ref_bnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> According to Article 13 of the Charter of Leningrad Oblast, the government bodies of the oblast are located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>. However, St. Petersburg is not officially named to be the administrative center of the oblast.</p>
<p><b>c.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cnone"><a href="#ref_cnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> According to Article 24 of the Charter of Moscow Oblast, the government bodies of the oblast are located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and throughout the territory of Moscow Oblast. However, Moscow is not officially named to be the administrative center of the oblast.</p>
<p><b>d.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_dnone"><a href="#ref_dnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea" title="Political status of Crimea">Not recognized internationally</a> as a part of Russia.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mergers">Mergers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Federal_subjects_of_Russia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mergers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Subjects_merged.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="905" data-file-width="1130" height="601" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Russian_Subjects_merged.png/750px-Russian_Subjects_merged.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Russian_Subjects_merged.png/1125px-Russian_Subjects_merged.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Russian_Subjects_merged.png 2x" width="750"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Subjects_merged.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Federal subjects of Russia</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Starting in 2005, some of the federal subjects were merged into larger territories<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="(February 2015)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup>. The merging process was finished on March 1, 2008. No new mergers have been planned since March 2008.</p>

<td><a href="/wiki/Chita_Oblast" title="Chita Oblast">Chita Oblast</a> (5) + <a href="/wiki/Agin-Buryat_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Agin-Buryat Autonomous Okrug">Agin-Buryat Autonomous Okrug</a> (5a)</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Zabaykalsky_Krai" title="Zabaykalsky Krai">Zabaykalsky Krai</a></td>
</tr>
</table>

epis2002.ru%2Fct%2Fhtml%2FTOM_01_04_1.htm&amp;rft.jtitle=%3Cspan+lang%3D%22ru%22++%3E%D0%92%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F+%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%8C+%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F+2002+%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%B0%3C%2Fspan%3ECategory%3AArticles+containing+Russian-language+text+%28All-Russia+Population+Census+of+2002%29&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span <li><span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">12 декабря 1993 г. «<a class="external text" href="http://www.consultant.ru/online/base/?req=doc;base=LAW;n=83686" rel="nofollow">Конституция Российской Федерации</a>», в ред. Опубликован: "Российская газета", №237, 25 декабря 1993 г.</span> (December 12, 1993 <i><a class="external text" href="http://translate.google.com/translate?hl=en&amp;sl=ru&amp;tl=en&amp;u=http://www.consultant.ru/online/base/?req=doc;base=LAW;n=83686" rel="nofollow">Constitution of the Russian Federation</a></i>, as amended by the Federal Constitutional Law #7-FKZ of December 30, 2008.
